| 2026-05-14 | e48a8028 | **Tier-Ω.5.f: class declarations + expressions, extends, super, instance methods, static methods, constructors, `new` (16 acceptance tests)** — closes the dominant remaining compiler gap that blocked any meaningful consumer-fixture run; every framework (Express, Hono, EventEmitter subclasses, error-type hierarchies) is dense with class definitions and pre-5.f they hit `CompileError("statement form not yet supported")` at the first `class Counter { ... }`. Post-5.f: classes lower to function + prototype + property installation per ECMA-262 §15.7; `new` consults `callee.prototype` to set the instance's `[[Prototype]]`; `instanceof` walks the chain; super-call + super.method dispatch via lexical hidden bindings. **Bytecode surface adds `Op::SetPrototype = 0x84`** (no operand, pops `[target, proto]`; sets `target.[[Prototype]] = proto` when proto is Object, `None` when Null) — the load-bearing engine primitive for wiring `proto.[[Prototype]] = Super.prototype` and `ctor.[[Prototype]] = Super` at class-creation time. `Op::Instanceof = 0x39` was reserved by the bytecode design but unwired; now implemented as the canonical walk: read `ctor.prototype` (own + proto-chain), walk `obj.proto` chain looking for that exact ObjectId. **Compiler change** (compiler.rs ~+260 LOC): `Stmt::ClassDecl` and `Expr::Class` both lower via a shared `compile_class(span, name, super_class, members)`. Strategy: allocate hidden locals `<class$N.super.ctor>`, `<class$N.super.proto>`, `<class$N.proto>`, `<class$N.ctor>` (unique per `class_seq` counter so nested classes don't collide); evaluate `extends` clause into `<super.ctor>`, derive `<super.proto>` via `GetProp "prototype"`; allocate prototype object via `NewObject`; wire `proto.[[Prototype]] = <super.proto>` via `SetPrototype` (for instance-method inheritance through the existing object_get chain walk); compile the constructor body (explicit if present, synthetic no-op otherwise) as an ordinary function proto, `MakeClosure` it, capture upvalues, bind to `<ctor>`; write `ctor.prototype = <proto>` and `proto.constructor = <ctor>` via `SetProp`; wire `ctor.[[Prototype]] = <super.ctor>` via `SetPrototype` (for static-method inheritance via the same chain walk against the constructor function object); for each instance method install onto `<proto>` via `SetProp`, each static method onto `<ctor>`. Default constructor when absent is a zero-param no-op (with or without `extends`): instance-method tests (#7, #13) call `new B()` without args; explicit constructor tests (#10) supply their own; no `...rest` synthesis needed at this surface. **Op::New now consults callee.prototype** (interp.rs:`Op::New`): if the callee is an Object whose `"prototype"` property resolves to another Object, the new instance is allocated with that as its `proto` instead of the default object_prototype auto-wire — this is the single load-bearing engine change that makes user-defined classes work with `new`. Regular `function Foo() {}` calls still get object_prototype because their closure has no `prototype` property, preserving pre-5.f behavior for non-class constructors. **Lowering route chosen for super.method: the upvalue route, not HomeObject.** When the class lowering site allocates `<super.proto>` as a real local in the outer compiler's `locals`, methods compiled as nested function protos see it as an enclosing local via `resolve_upvalue` and capture it through the existing Ω.5.c machinery — no `home_object` field added to `ClosureInternals`, no new opcode, no runtime change. The class-emission site already had to allocate hidden locals for `<proto>` and `<ctor>` regardless; piggy-backing `<super.proto>` and `<super.ctor>` onto the same allocation was strictly cheaper than introducing a `Op::GetHomeProto` opcode + a `home_object: Option<ObjectId>` field. The HomeObject route's advantage (matching ECMA-262 §13.3.7 verbatim) doesn't pay off until method-shorthand object literals (`{ method() {} }`) need super-references too — at which point `<super.proto>` isn't lexically available because there's no enclosing class context. Defer the HomeObject migration to whenever method shorthand on object literals lands (out of scope this round). **`class_stack: Vec<ClassFrame>` on Compiler** carries `(super_ctor_name, super_proto_name, in_constructor, is_static)` and is cloned into the sub-compiler in `compile_function_proto`. `Expr::Call` with callee `Expr::Super` lowers to a `CallMethod` with `PushThis` as receiver and the captured `<super.ctor>` as method (so the parent constructor sees the current instance as `this`, which is what the subclass constructor's `Op::New`-allocated `this` is). `Expr::Member` with object `Expr::Super` resolves against `<super.proto>` in instance-method context, `<super.ctor>` in static-method context (test #12 multi-level static inheritance). `super(...)` is rejected outside a derived-class constructor; `super.x` is rejected outside a class with `extends`. **No ClosureInternals field added** — the upvalue route was strictly contained. **Substrate-amortization signal**: this round was the cleanest compiler-amortization since Ω.5.a. The class lowering does *no* new runtime allocation, *no* new InternalKind, *no* new value variant. The prototype-chain `object_get` walk (existed since Ω.5.a), the prototype-aware `Op::New`, and the `instanceof` chain walk all reuse the same primitive: `obj.proto` is the substrate, every class-instance / inherited-method / instanceof-check / super-method-dispatch is a closure-site reading that substrate. The `Op::SetPrototype` opcode is the only new primitive and it's a 3-line interpreter handler. Class declarations are a closure site over `Op::New + object_get + alloc_object`. **Acceptance bar (16/16 pass, 0 defer)**: 1. empty class typeof === "object" ✓ 2. constructor with args → `c.a + c.b === 3` ✓ 3. instance method `new C().greet() === "hi"` ✓ 4. method using `this` with state accumulation `c.inc()` x3 → 3 ✓ 5. multiple methods coexisting ✓ 6. static method `C.who() === "C"` ✓ 7. extends without overriding → parent method inherited ✓ 8. extends with override → child method takes precedence ✓ 9. `super.method()` returns parent's value composed with child's ✓ 10. `super(args)` in subclass constructor binds parent's instance state ✓ 11. `b instanceof B && b instanceof A` via prototype-chain walk ✓ 12. static inheritance `B.who() === "A"` via ctor's proto chain ✓ 13. multi-level inheritance A → B → C, `new C().f() === 1` ✓ 14. anonymous class expression ✓ 15. named class expression ✓ 16. EventEmitter-style: bus.on(h1); bus.on(h2); bus.emit(10) → 31 (handlers stored on `this.handlers`, called in order with the arg) ✓. **Deferred (explicit re-open conditions noted in scope ceiling)**: private fields `#x`, public class fields `x = 0`, static initializer blocks `static { ... }`, computed method names `{ [expr]() {} }`, generator methods, async methods, getter/setter shorthand, `new.target`. | 2026-05-14 | b070aca1 | **Tier-Ω.5.g.1: per-iteration fresh binding for `let`/`const` in for-of (ECMA-262 §14.7.5.5) — 5 acceptance tests, pure-closure round.** Closes the lone deferred item from Ω.5.e (t10) and the first of three surfaces identified by the Ω.5.g.0 probe. Pre-Ω.5.g.1: `const cs = []; for (const i of [1,2,3]) cs.push(() => i); cs.map(f=>f())` returned `[3,3,3]` because the compiler allocated one `bind_slot` before the for-of loop and `StoreLocal`'d into it each iteration — closures captured the slot's promoted cell, so all three closures shared the same cell holding the last iteration's value. Post-Ω.5.g.1: returns `[1,2,3]` per spec. **Route chosen: A (fresh-cell-reset), not B (IIFE-wrap).** Per Ω.5.g.0 probe: A is more spec-aligned because the body executes in the for-of frame, preserving break/continue/return/yield semantics; B's function-call-per-iteration overhead is real and the IIFE wrapper synthesizes a function frame that interferes with future generator (`yield`) and labelled-break/continue lowering. **New opcode `Op::ResetLocalCell = 0x19`** (u16 operand: slot index): clears `frame.local_cells[slot]` to `None` so the next `CaptureLocal` at that slot's `promote_local` call allocates a fresh `UpvalueCell`. Existing closures that already captured the previous cell retain their `Rc<RefCell<Value>>` handle — only the frame's binding to the cell is severed. Three-line interpreter handler in `interp.rs`: decode u16, bounds-check, set `local_cells[slot] = None`. **Compiler change** (compiler.rs ~+15 LOC, in the `Stmt::ForOf` arm at lines 317-388): the bind-slot allocation now also tracks `per_iter_fresh: bool` — true when the head is `ForBinding::Decl { kind: Let | Const, .. }`, false for `kind: Var` (var stays function-scoped and shared per §14.7.5.5) and false for `ForBinding::Identifier` (pre-existing binding from outer scope, not the for-of head). At iteration entry, right after `GetProp "value"` and before `StoreLocal bind_slot`, when `per_iter_fresh` is true, emit `Op::ResetLocalCell <bind_slot>`. The subsequent `StoreLocal` takes the non-promoted `write_local` path (since `local_cells[slot]` is None) and writes directly to `locals[slot]`; when the body's `MakeClosure → CaptureLocal` runs, `promote_local` moves `locals[slot]` into a fresh `UpvalueCell` distinct from the prior iteration's. Op-pattern membership and `op_from_byte` updated; `disasm.rs` doesn't need changes (ResetLocalCell uses a slot index, not a constant index, so the default operand rendering applies and the const_resolved match arm is correctly absent for it). **Substrate-amortization signal: pure-closure as the Ω.5.g.0 probe predicted.** Total delta: ~3 lines op.rs (enum variant + operand-size + op_from_byte) + 1 line disasm.rs (none required) + 11 lines interp.rs (handler) + 15 lines compiler.rs (per_iter_fresh tracking + emit), no AST changes, no parser changes, no runtime data-structure changes, no value-variant additions, no `ClosureInternals` field additions. The Ω.5.e `Frame.local_cells: Vec<Option<UpvalueCell>>` substrate (where `None` already meant "not yet promoted") was the exact mechanism required — `ResetLocalCell` reverts a slot to "not yet promoted" state and the next iteration's CaptureLocal naturally promotes again. **Acceptance bar (5/5 pass)**: 1. canonical `const cs = []; for (const i of [1,2,3]) cs.push(() => i); cs[0]()+","+cs[1]()+","+cs[2]() === "1,2,3"` ✓ 2. same with `let i` head ✓ 3. `var i` head returns `"3,3,3"` (var is function-scoped, shared — locks in the var-vs-let distinction so we don't accidentally per-iteration-promote a var) ✓ 4. `continue` mid-loop when `i === 2` → first/third closures return 1 and 3 (only iterations that survive to MakeClosure capture their cell) ✓ 5. `break` after `i === 2` → first two closures return 1 and 2 (break exits but the closures already captured their iterations' cells) ✓. The Ω.5.e t10 ignored test (`#[ignore = "deferred: per-iteration binding for let/const in for-of is a compiler-side concern, not solved by Tier-Ω.5.e runtime upvalue migration"]`) was unignored and now passes; comment updated to cite Tier-Ω.5.g.1 + the ResetLocalCell mechanism. **Out of scope (explicit re-open conditions)**: C-style `for (let i = 0; i < n; i++)` also requires per-iteration binding per ECMA-262 §14.7.4.2 but the lowering is different (the init binding becomes the per-iteration source via a copy-then-rebind step); deferred to Ω.5.g.4 candidate. `for-in` with `let`/`const` head: same deferral. Multi-name destructuring head (`for (const [a,b] of ...)`) deferred to Ω.5.g.3 (depends on destructuring substrate to be introduced by Ω.5.g.2 in the main session). **Test counts**: rusty-js-runtime binding_capture.rs 11 passing + 1 ignored → 16 passing + 0 ignored (+5 net passing, the t10 unignore + 4 new t10b/c/d/e). Workspace 677 passing in host integration unchanged, 4 pre-existing baseline failures (express ×2, stringz, winston) unchanged, ignored count drops by 1 (the unignored t10). Disk free at end: 110M (started 1.7G per the spec; the bytecode + runtime + dependents rebuild consumed it; **no `cargo clean` per discipline**, well under ENOSPC). Phase classification: substrate-amortization closure round on Ω.5.e's `Frame.local_cells: Vec<Option<UpvalueCell>>` — the `None`-means-unpromoted invariant was the exact substrate; this round closes one more closure site over it. Sets up Ω.5.g.2 (main-session substrate for destructure + template interpolation), which will then enable Ω.5.g.3 (destructuring for-of heads) as a second closure site. |

Array rest uses runtime helper `__destr_array_rest(src, start)` (installed in intrinsics.rs alongside parseInt/etc, ~25 LOC); object rest uses `__destr_object_rest(src, excluded_keys_array)` (~30 LOC). The first quasi is always a String constant (possibly empty), which seeds the chain into the String-coercion path on the first Add and every subsequent Add inherits it. Verified by `t05_mixed_types`: `` `n=${5}, s=${"hi"}, b=${true}` `` produces `"n=5, s=hi, b=true"`. **Helper-vs-inline choice for rest**: helpers chosen. Rationale: array-rest's inline-bytecode variant would need a length-loop with a per-iteration GetIndex + InitIndex, requiring a back-jump pattern inside an expression-position emission site (no existing pattern for that — the for-of and for/while emitters all operate at statement level); object-rest's inline variant would need an enumeration opcode the bytecode design doesn't have. Two `__`-prefixed globals are cheaper than two new opcodes plus the bytecode-level enumeration primitive — and the helpers are testable as ordinary intrinsics. The `__`-prefix advertises that these are engine-internal, the same convention as the pre-existing `__record` test-record intrinsic. **Substrate-amortization signal: substrate did its job.** Closure round, exactly as Ω.5.g.2's spec predicted. Zero new opcodes (the InitIndex + NewArray + LoadGlobal + Call composition was already there); zero new AST nodes (everything composed against Ω.5.g.2's BindingPattern/BindingElement/PropertyKey + TemplateLiteral.quasis/.expressions); two ~25-LOC runtime helpers in intrinsics.rs. `BindingPattern::collect_names` was the single load-bearing scope-binding helper — declarator/for-of-head/parameter paths all pre-allocate leaf locals via it before destructure emission, so the recursive walk can do a simple `resolve_local(&id.name)` for each leaf store. Pre-Ω.5.h: compiler errored at the `ExportDeclaration::Named { source: Some(_) } | StarFrom | StarAsFrom` branch (compiler.rs:319 in the Ω.5.b vintage). Post-Ω.5.h: all four forms compile and the runtime populates the namespace by reading from eagerly-loaded source modules. **AST was ready** (Ω.5.g.2-vintage): `ExportDeclaration::Named { source: Some, specifiers }`, `StarFrom`, `StarAsFrom { exported }`, and `ExportSpecifier { imported: ModuleExportName, exported: ModuleExportName }` carry every name including `default`. **Bytecode-table widening** (rusty-js-bytecode/derived/src/compiler.rs): `ExportBinding` migrated from a single `{ exported: String, local: u16 }` struct to a four-variant enum — `Local { exported, local }` (existing), `Named { exported, source_specifier, imported }`, `Star { source_specifier }`, `StarAs { exported, source_specifier }`. `CompiledModule` gains a `reexport_sources: Vec<String>` field collecting every `from "..."` specifier so the runtime can load them eagerly. The compiler's three new `compile_export` arms each: (a) push the specifier into `reexport_sources` (deduplicated by linear scan), (b) emit one `ExportBinding::Named` per spec for Named-with-source (with imported/exported names extracted from `ModuleExportName::{Ident, String}`), one `Star` for StarFrom, or one `StarAs` for StarAsFrom. Default↔named conversions fall out for free: `export { default as x } from` lowers to `Named { exported: "x", imported: "default" }`, and `export { x as default } from` to `Named { exported: "default", imported: "x" }` — the runtime reads source.namespace[imported] and writes this.namespace[exported] with no special-casing. **Runtime change** (rusty-js-runtime/derived/src/module.rs `evaluate_module`): between import-resolution and body-execution, walk `bytecode_rc.reexport_sources` and load each (file or `node:*`) into a local `HashMap<String, ObjectRef>` keyed by the original specifier text — the same string that survives onto each `ExportBinding::Named/Star/StarAs.source_specifier`. The namespace-build phase then case-splits on the variant: Local reads from `frame.locals[local]` (unchanged); Named reads `object_get(src_ns, imported)` and writes under `exported`; Star snapshots source's `properties` map (via `&self.obj(src_ns)`), filters out `"default"` per ECMA-262 §16.2.3.7, and copies each remaining `(key, value)` pair into the receiving namespace; StarAs writes `Value::Object(src_ns)` under `exported`. The Star snapshot is a deliberate borrow-checker dance — extracting `Vec<(String, Value)>` before the mutation loop releases the `&Object` borrow so `object_set` can take `&mut self`. **Substrate-amortization signal: pure-closure round, prediction held exactly.** Zero new opcodes, zero new AST nodes, zero new runtime data structures. The widening of `ExportBinding` from struct to enum is the entire shape change; everything else composes against Ω.5.b's `Runtime::load_module` (eager source resolution), `resolve_builtin_namespace` (`node:*` re-exports too), `Runtime::modules` cache (snapshot semantics: a re-export source that's still `Linking` returns its partial namespace, matching the cyclic-import behavior locked in Ω.5.b), `object_get` (default↔named lookup), and `Object.properties: HashMap` (Star's own-key enumeration). The only call-site outside the new code that needed updating was `resolve_builtin_namespace`'s synthetic `CompiledModule { ... }` construction, which gained `reexport_sources: Vec::new()` alongside the existing imports/exports empties — strictly mechanical. **Cycle handling**: snapshot semantics per Ω.5.b. If a re-export source module is still in `ModuleStatus::Linking` when the namespace-build phase runs, the recursive `load_module` call returns the partially-populated namespace ObjectRef (per Ω.5.b's existing logic); Star's snapshot then copies whatever keys are present. Spec-faithful live-binding behavior for re-exports is deferred — when the source later evaluates an additional export, the importer's namespace won't see it. Documented in module.rs's banner update. **Acceptance bar (8/8 pass)**: 1. Named re-export `export { add } from "./mod.mjs"` consumer calls `add()` ✓ 2. Named re-export with rename `export { add as sum } from` consumer imports `sum` ✓ 3. Star re-export `export * from "./mod.mjs"` consumer imports each of a/b/c ✓ 4. Star skips default — source has both `named` and `export default`; star-reexporter's `import * as ns` shows `ns.named` defined and `typeof ns.default === "undefined"` per §16.2.3.7 ✓ 5. Star-as re-export `export * as utils from`; consumer `utils.add(2,3) === 5` ✓ 6. Default re-export `export { default } from`; consumer's default import is the function ✓ 7. Default-to-named `export { default as add } from`; consumer's `import { add }` works ✓ 8. Named-to-default `export { add as default } from`; consumer's default import calls the source's named binding ✓. **Out of scope (explicit defer)**: live bindings for re-exports (snapshot v1 only — same deferral as Ω.5.b's imports); circular re-export "exhausted"/non-converging detection (the spec's TypeError; v1 may produce undefined values without erroring); the standalone `export { x }` (no `from`) path is unchanged and still uses `Local`. **Test counts**: rusty-js-runtime gains tests/re_exports.rs (8 passing). Touched-crate aggregate: rusty-js-ast + rusty-js-parser + rusty-js-bytecode + rusty-js-runtime totals 507 passing / 0 failed; rusty-bun-host integration totals 679 passing + 4 pre-existing baseline failures (express ×2, stringz, winston — Ω.5.a-vintage, unchanged) + 16 ignored. Workspace `cargo test --no-fail-fast` aggregate prior to a timeout on the web-crypto verifier slice: 1890 passing / 4 failing — the 4 are the same baseline, and the web-crypto verifier was killed at ~11min CPU-saturated (sleeping in syscall) for orthogonal reasons (RSA/EC keygen on the Pi); not related to this round. **Disk free at end**: rootfs 1.8G, T7 1.4T — target redirected to T7 throughout, no rootfs pressure. **No `cargo clean`**, no `.cargo/config.toml` override. **Phase classification**: substrate-amortization closure round on Ω.5.b's module-loader substrate, exactly per Doc 714 §VI Consequence 7's healthy-signal — every primitive needed (eager source loading via `load_module`, `node:*` via `resolve_builtin_namespace`, snapshot cycles via the pre-populated namespace ObjectRef on the Linking record, `Object.properties` enumeration for Star) was already in place from Ω.5.b. The parity-failure-bin delta (post-Ω.5.h re-run not executed this round) is bounded by the 26 packages that had been failing with the re-export CompileError; whether they now pass depends on whether each has additional unrelated gaps. Eligible re-runs of `/tmp/parity-host-v2-static.sh` will move 0/118 → ≤26 packages out of the re-export bin, with the residual distribution informing the next round's target. |

The post-Ω.5.h parity dig had identified this as the single highest-leverage residual gap, accounting for 25 of 32 "expression form" failures across real packages (acorn, pluralize, minimatch, decimal.js, ansi-colors, change-case, magic-string, etc.). Post-Ω.5.i: regex literals lower through the engine end-to-end and the runtime exposes the canonical instance method surface. **AST widening** (rusty-js-ast/src/lib.rs): `Expr::RegExp { pattern: Rc<String>, flags: Rc<String>, span }` added next to `TemplateLiteral`; `Expr::span()`'s exhaustive match extended. **Parser change** (rusty-js-parser/derived/src/expr.rs ~+5 LOC): the Opaque branch at expr.rs:494-498 replaced with direct construction from the token's `body` and `flags` fields, both wrapped in `Rc::new`. **Compiler lowering route chosen: `__createRegExp` helper, not `Op::NewRegExp` opcode.** Trades one bytecode slot for one symbol-table entry at install_intrinsics time. Rationale: the existing `LoadGlobal + PushConst + PushConst + Call 2` composition is already a tested path (every `parseInt(s, r)` call lowers this way); adding `Op::NewRegExp` would require a new dispatch arm in `interp.rs`'s opcode dispatch with no payoff vs. the helper. ~12 LOC in `compile_expr`'s new `Expr::RegExp` arm: intern pattern + flags as String constants, emit `LoadGlobal __createRegExp; PushConst pat; PushConst flags; Call 2`. **Runtime substrate** (rusty-js-runtime, ~520 LOC new file `regexp.rs` + value.rs + interp.rs + Cargo.toml + lib.rs + intrinsics.rs edits): `InternalKind::RegExp(RegExpInternals { source: Rc<String>, flags: Rc<String>, compiled: Option<regex::Regex>, last_index: usize })` added next to `Promise`; `regex = "1"` added to runtime Cargo.toml. `Runtime` gains `regexp_prototype: Option<ObjectId>`; the alloc-time proto-wire seam in `alloc_object` extended to map `InternalKind::RegExp(_) -> regexp_prototype`, exactly the same pattern as Array/Promise/Function from Ω.5.a. `install_regexp` runs from `install_intrinsics` between `install_promise` and `install_test_record`; it allocates the prototype, installs `.test` / `.exec` / `.toString` via `register_method`, registers the `__createRegExp` and `RegExp` globals, and finally extends `string_prototype` with regex-aware `.match` / `.search` / `.replace` / `.replaceAll` / `.split` — overwriting the pre-existing string-only `.replace` and `.split` from prototype.rs at the same property slot. **Pattern translation** (regexp.rs `translate`): JS `i`/`m`/`s` flags map to Rust's `(?ims)` inline-flag prefix; `g` (global) and `y` (sticky) are no-ops at the regex compile layer — consumed at the API level via `last_index` for `g`'s stateful exec; `u` (unicode) and `d` (indices) are accepted as no-ops because the Rust regex crate is unicode-default and v1 doesn't emit match-offset arrays. Compilation failures (lookbehind, backreferences, named groups in incompatible syntax) are non-fatal: `compiled = None`, and method calls then throw a TypeError naming the offending source. Documented as v1 deviation. **Real-world sample**: 8 representative patterns from `decimal.js`, `pluralize`, `minimatch`, `change-case`, `ansi-colors`, `acorn`, `magic-string`, plus a word-boundary alt-group all compile cleanly through `translate` (verified out-of-band in a scratch crate against `regex 1.12`). Zero needed `compiled = None`. **Prototype method semantics**: `.test(s)` runs `is_match` on the compiled regex. `.exec(s)` per ECMA-262 §22.2.5.2: returns `null` on no match; otherwise an Array with `[match, ...captures]`, an `.index` property (char offset, not byte), and `.input`. Under the `g` flag the receiver's `last_index` advances to the match's byte-end, and both the in-memory `RegExpInternals.last_index` field and the JS-visible `.lastIndex` own-property are mutated. The captures snapshot is a deliberate borrow-checker dance — `captures_at(&input, start)` borrows the regex immutably, the match positions and groups are collected into owned Strings, then the borrow is released so `alloc_object` and `object_set` can take `&mut self`. **String.prototype regex-aware methods** all use a shared `coerce_regexp` that returns the receiver's id when it's already a RegExp or constructs a fresh one with empty flags when it's a string. `.replace` and `.replaceAll` share `string_replace_impl(force_global)` which case-splits replacement: string → `regex::Regex::replace_all` / `replacen`; function → collect match ranges, then iterate calling `rt.call_function(repl, Undefined, [Value::String(match)])` and stitching the result. Spec-faithful `$1` backref substitution in replace strings is deferred — the Rust regex crate's `Replacer` trait does support `$N` but in a different syntax (`${name}`); v1 treats replacement strings as literals to keep the deviation explicit. **Constructor form** (`new RegExp(p, f)` and `RegExp(p, f)`): both registered as the same global `RegExp`, routing through `new_regexp(rt, &p, &f)` — identical to the literal path. If the first arg is already a RegExp, source and flags are read from its internals and a fresh instance is allocated. **Substrate-amortization signal: substrate-introduction round, prediction held exactly.** New shape introduced: AST variant + InternalKind variant + Runtime field + crate dep + prototype slot + helper global. (3) `Runtime::evaluate_cjs_module(source, url)` — synthesizes a wrapper at the source level: `export default (function (exports, module, require, __filename, __dirname) {\n<source>\n});`, parses + compiles via the existing ESM pipeline, runs the outer module body, extracts the wrapper-function value from the "<module.default>" local slot, allocates `module = {exports: {}}` + `exports = module.exports`, builds a per-module `require` NativeFn closure capturing the requiring module's URL, then calls the wrapper with the synthesized argument tuple. Final `module.exports` is read back as the canonical exports value (handles rebind via `module.exports = X` correctly — both rebind-to-object and rebind-to-primitive/function paths pass). A "namespace view" ObjectRef is synthesized on the same allocation (mirrors `module.exports` own properties when it's an object, sets `default` to the exports value either way) so ESM `import * as X from "./lib.cjs"` and existing `import lib from "./lib.cjs"` callsites both work. (4) `Runtime::cjs_require(parent_url, spec)` — first probes the ResolveBuiltinModule host hook with the spec as-is, then with `node:` prefix when the spec is unprefixed (so `require("fs")` and `require("node:fs")` both succeed); for relative / `file://` specifiers consults the module cache (returns `cjs_exports` for CJS, namespace for ESM), then dispatches to `load_module`; bare specifiers error cleanly (node_modules walk-up deferred). **ESM-importing-CJS dispatch** lives in `evaluate_module`'s import-resolution loop: after `load_module` returns, `cjs_exports_of(resolved)` queries whether the target is CJS; if so, `Default` returns `module.exports` directly (raw value, so `module.exports = 42` binds the importer's default to 42), `Named(n)` reads `object_get(module.exports, n)` if it's an object (else TypeError with a clear message), `Namespace` builds a synthesized namespace view. **Host-v2 resolver extended**: `install_builtin_module_resolver` now matches both `node:fs|path|os|process` and the unprefixed forms `fs|path|os|process`, so the engine-side cjs_require doesn't need to know which names the host owns. **Source-concat wrapper approach was the right call**: dropped in cleanly with zero parser/compiler shape changes. The wrapper compiles as ordinary ESM whose `export default <FunctionExpression>` is already supported (Tier-Ω.5.b machinery). The wrapper function is extracted from the resulting module's exports local slot using the existing `ExportBinding::Local` table — no new bytecode op, no new AST node, no new compiler entry point. **v1 deviation: line-number off-by-one in CJS error spans** — the wrapper's leading `export default (function (exports, module, require, __filename, __dirname) {\n` adds one newline, so all CJS error messages report line N+1 against the user's original source. AST was already shape-ready: `ObjectProperty::Spread { expr, span }` and `Argument::Spread { expr, span }` (rusty-js-ast/src/lib.rs ~lines 150 + 168), introduced earlier this engagement. This round closes both surfaces. **Lowering route — object literal**: chose the `__object_spread(target, src)` helper variant over re-routing through `Object.assign`. The helper is one `register_global_fn` call at install_intrinsics time, copies `src`'s own-enumerable string-keyed properties onto `target`, and is a no-op when `src` is null/undefined. Compiler emit (pilots/rusty-js-bytecode/derived/src/compiler.rs `Expr::Object` arm, Spread case): `Dup; LoadGlobal __object_spread; Swap; <compile src>; Call 2; Pop` — stack invariant `[target] → [target]`, left-to-right merge order preserved by the existing properties iteration. **Lowering route — spread args**: chose `__apply(callee, this, argsArray)` helper over a new `Op::CallSpread` opcode. The argsArray is constructed inline via `__array_push_single(arr, v)` for Expr arguments and `__array_extend(arr, iter)` for Spread arguments; the latter routes through the existing `collect_iterable` (`@@iterator` protocol from Ω.5.c), so any iterable source composes — not just Arrays. Compiler emit (compiler.rs `Expr::Call` arm + `emit_args_array` helper): plain call `f(...args)` lowers to `LoadGlobal __apply; <callee>; PushUndef; <argsArray>; Call 3`; method call `obj.f(...args)` to `LoadGlobal __apply; <obj>; Dup; GetProp f; Swap; <argsArray>; Call 3` (receiver becomes `this` for the method); super calls thread `PushThis` as the receiver and the parent ctor / prototype's method as the callable. `new C(...args)` routes through a parallel `__construct(callee, argsArray)` helper that mirrors `Op::New`'s semantics — consults `callee.prototype` for the new instance's `[[Prototype]]`, calls with the instance as `this`, and discards non-object returns per ECMA-262 §10.2.1.2. **Helper count: five new NativeFns** (`__object_spread`, `__array_push_single`, `__array_extend`, `__apply`, `__construct`), all installed in a new `install_spread_helpers` block in `intrinsics.rs` between `install_destructure_helpers` and `install_globals`. **Substrate-amortization signal: pure-closure round, prediction held exactly.** Zero new AST nodes, zero new opcodes, zero new runtime data structures. | 2026-05-14 | 36e7c728 | **Tier-Ω.5.q: bare specifier resolution + node_modules walk-up + package.json exports (12 acceptance tests, substrate-introduction round per seed §A8.13).** Closes the largest single bin in the post-Ω.5.p parity reading: `Rt:bare-spec` carried 17 direct + transitive packages, all gated on the explicit `TypeError("bare specifier '...' is not supported in v1 (node_modules walk and package.json resolution are deferred)")` from Ω.5.b. This round wires the surface. **Substrate added** (4 surfaces): (1) `Runtime::resolve_module_full(parent_url, specifier, importer_kind: ModuleKind)` — the importer-kind-aware resolver; non-bare specifiers (`node:`, `./`, `../`, `file://`) delegate to the existing free helper `Runtime::resolve_module`, bare specifiers run the new walk-up + package.json pipeline. The new `importer_kind` parameter threads ESM-vs-CJS so an ESM `import` picks the `exports` conditional-resolution priority `import → node → default` while a CJS `require` picks `require → node → default`. ESM `evaluate_module`'s import-resolution loop and re-export-source-load loop both switch to `self.resolve_module_full(url, spec, ModuleKind::ESM)`; `cjs_require` calls it with `ModuleKind::CJS`. (2) `ParsedPackageJson` struct + `Runtime::read_package_json(path)` method with a `pkg_json_cache: HashMap<PathBuf, Rc<ParsedPackageJson>>` field on `Runtime`. Each package.json is parsed once via `serde_json` (promoted from transitive-only to a direct dep of rusty-js-runtime; already pinned at 1.0.149 in workspace Cargo.lock so the promotion is a one-line manifest add, no new download required). The cache is never invalidated — filesystem changes during a single process run are out-of-scope for v1. (3) `split_bare_specifier(specifier) -> Option<(pkg_name, subpath)>` — handles plain (`react` → `("react", "")`, `lodash/fp/get` → `("lodash", "./fp/get")`) and scoped (`@org/pkg` → `("@org/pkg", "")`, `@org/pkg/sub` → `("@org/pkg", "./sub")`) names. Empty / malformed inputs return None. (4) `walk_up_for_pkg(start_dir, pkg_name)` + `resolve_within_package(pkg_dir, pkg, subpath, importer_kind)` + `resolve_exports_target(target, capture, importer_kind)` — the resolution algorithm proper. Walk-up scans from `dirname(parent_url)` (or the URL itself when it's already a dir) upward, returning the first existing `node_modules/<pkg_name>` directory. Within-package resolution: empty subpath consults `exports."."` (or top-level conditional map when `exports` keys don't start with `.`), then falls back to `module` (ESM importer only) → `main` → `index.<ext>` via the existing extension-probe chain. Subpath imports try exact `exports."./X"`, then any key with a `*` wildcard (matching prefix + suffix and substituting the captured middle into the target's `*`), then the literal subpath relative to the package directory. Conditional-export resolution is recursive: strings substitute the wildcard capture and return verbatim, arrays try first-success, objects walk the priority list. Conditions explicitly skipped: `browser`, `types`, `react-native`, `deno`, `worker` (per locked-design scope ceiling). JSON-target resolution returns a clear deferral error pointing at the JSON-modules out-of-scope ceiling. **Acceptance bar 12/12 pass** in `pilots/rusty-js-runtime/derived/tests/bare_specifier.rs`: t01 simple bare ESM via `main` + `type:module` ✓; t02 `module` field preferred for ESM over `main:.cjs` ✓; t03 `exports.".".import` condition picks the ESM target over the CJS target ✓; t04 `exports.".".default` fallback when no `import` or `require` keys present ✓; t05 subpath `import { x } from "foo/sub"` via `exports."./sub":"./lib/sub.js"` ✓; t06 wildcard pattern `exports."./fp/*":"./dist/fp/*.js"` resolves `foo/fp/get` to `./dist/fp/get.js` ✓; t07 scoped `@org/pkg` resolves correctly ✓; t08 walk-up from an entry two directories deep finds workspace-root node_modules ✓; t09 `pkg_json_cache` is populated after one import (verified by HashMap key presence) ✓; t10 CJS `require('foo')` picks the `require` condition over `import` ✓; t11 ESM `import foo from "foo"` where foo's `main` is a `.cjs` reads `module.exports` per the existing Ω.5.j.cjs ESM-importing-CJS interop ✓; t12 unresolved bare spec produces a TypeError naming the specifier ✓. **Test counts**: rusty-js-runtime 369 → 381 passing (+12), 0 failed. Workspace baseline holds (853 passing + 4 baseline consumer-regression failures — express ×2, stringz, winston — unchanged through the runtime crate). **Post-round parity reading** (rebuild rusty-bun-host-v2 + rerun /tmp/parity-host-v2-static.sh): **n_ok 23/118 → 23/119 (19.3% → 19.3%)** — sandbox grew by one package, OK count held. The `Rt:bare-spec` bin reduced **17 → 8** (-9 packages exited that bin). Those 9 packages migrated into deeper-stage failure bins: `CE:other` 49 → 50 (+1), `CE:expression` 8 → 10 (+2), `Rt:TypeError` 21 → 26 (+5), with the remainder distributed across the smaller bins. **Snowball-progression signal**: same healthy pattern as Ω.5.o / Ω.5.p — closures land cleanly, the targeted bin drains, packages move one layer deeper, the OK column doesn't yet credit them because their next-stage gap is exposed. The bare-spec mass will resurface in the passing column once the bins it migrated into are also closed. The fact that the bare-spec bin didn't drain to zero (8 remaining) is the *transitive* effect: packages that NOW successfully resolve their entry bare-spec via this round's wiring may *import* a sub-dependency whose own bare-spec fails for a reason the current resolver doesn't handle (most likely: package.json without an `exports` field where `main` points to a file that doesn't exist verbatim — Node would extension-probe; our probe chain does, so this is worth a dig.sh follow-up). **Substrate-amortization signal**: matched the predicted shape exactly — substrate-introduction round, new helpers + new dep + new method, **no new opcodes, no AST changes, no new IR**. The compiler's import path was already wired through `resolve_module`; only the resolver internals changed. Pure additive surface: one new field on Runtime, one new method on Runtime (plus `read_package_json` private-ish helper), five free helper functions, one new struct. Promotion of `serde_json` from transitive-only to direct dep costs zero bytes on disk (already in Cargo.lock at 1.0.149 from another path) and avoids a hand-rolled JSON walker that would have duplicated `scan_package_type`'s tradeoffs at higher complexity. **v1 deviations documented**: (a) `imports` field (private package-internal aliases) not handled — packages using `imports` will get a clear error pointing at the deferral. (b) `browser`, `types`, `react-native`, `deno`, `worker` conditions all skipped. (c) Self-referential package imports (`import "self"` from inside the same package) not handled. (d) JSON modules return a clear deferral error. (e) WASM modules not considered. (f) pnpm's `.pnpm` symlink layout is technically still a node_modules tree from this resolver's perspective; symlink resolution edge cases not exercised. **Disk free at end**: rootfs 1.8G unchanged, T7 ample — target redirected via `.cargo/config.toml` throughout, no rootfs pressure. **No `cargo clean`**, no `.cargo/config.toml` override. **Phase classification**: substrate-introduction round per seed §A8.13 — the round expands the engine's contingent-decision inventory along module-resolution per Doc 714 §VI Consequence 8. Static private fields work the same way. v1 deviation: privacy isn't enforced — obj["#x"] reads from outside; spec-faithful WeakMap-backed privacy queued for a substrate round. Newly-surfaced gap (queued for Ω.5.x): static methods that reference the class binding by name (e.g. `static get() { return D.#count }`) fail because the class isn't bound in the method's scope at compile time. The pre-existing class-binding-in-method-body hoisting issue surfaces only now that private static fields exposed the pattern. Parity 26/119 unchanged at the surface (same Consequence 8 redistribution as Ω.5.u-v). |
| 2026-05-14 | (Ω.5.x) | **Tier-Ω.5.x: class-name binding visible inside method bodies + await as no-op (6 tests, main session)** — two closure surfaces, both pure-compiler. Surface 1: Stmt::ClassDecl pre-allocates the class name's local slot BEFORE compile_class emits the method bodies, so methods that reference the class by name (`static get() { return D.#count; }`) resolve `D` via upvalue capture. The slot is uninitialized at emission time but holds the constructor by the time any method actually runs. Closes the pattern bug surfaced by Ω.5.w's private-static-field smoke. Surface 2: `await expr` lowers as no-op (the argument's value passes through). v1 deviation: suspension semantics dropped; awaiting a Promise returns the Promise object itself, not its resolved value. Real consumer code that probes via shape inspection rarely drives past entry into actual async dispatch, so the no-op is sufficient to unblock module-namespace probes. Parity 26/119 → 27/119 (+1, 22.6%). |

| 2026-05-14 | (Ω.5.ee) | **Tier-Ω.5.ee: function-declaration hoisting** — per ECMA-262 §10.2.1.3 / §14.1.22. Dense CJS idiom `exports = module.exports = objectHash; ... function objectHash() {}` depends on hoisting. Implementation: two-phase per function body. H1 pre-allocates local slots for top-level var/let/const + function names so nested-function bodies' upvalue resolution finds them at compile time. H2 emits MakeClosure + StoreLocal for FunctionDecls into the pre-allocated slots before any other statement runs. VariableDecl compile path reuses pre-allocated slots via a `pre_allocated_slots` map. Without H1, hoisting `function inner() { return x }` would resolve x as a global at compile time (later `let x = ...` would be a fresh slot). Parity 41/119 → 43/119 (+2). |

| 2026-05-15 | 267b9d61 | **Tier-Ω.5.gg: export-declaration bodies routed through the typed statement parser; `for (id in obj)` bare-ident fast-path (10 template edge-case tests)** — substrate-introduction round (lexer-driver state machine semantics, not closure work). The Ω.5.ff observation that the residual tail was parser-bug-dominant reduced this round to a single locus. `parse_declaration_for_export` was walking `export function` / `export class` bodies with `skip_balanced(LBrace, RBrace)`, which counts raw brace punctuators with no knowledge of template-literal substitution boundaries: a body containing `` return `X: ${alg}`; `` lost the lexer's brace count when the substitution's closing `}` was treated as the function body's closing `}`, then leaked into subsequent statements and surfaced as UnterminatedTemplate at the next real backtick later in the file. **Diagnostic reduction**: minimal failing input is `` export function f(alg) { return `X: ${alg}`; } `` — without the `export` keyword (plain `function f`) it parses, because plain top-level FunctionDeclaration routes through `parse_function_decl_stmt` which calls `parse_function_body` → `parse_statement` → template-with-substitution through the proper lexer goal exchange. **Bug-reduction class**: neither Option A (lexer set_pos boundary mid-substitution) nor Option B (escaped-backtick handling in `read_string_escape`); the brief's two hypothesized loci were both correct in isolation. The defect lived one layer up — in an export-decl shortcut that bypassed the proper parser/lexer goal-driven loop. Recording this as the **third hypothesis category** for future template-bin chases: upstream parser shortcuts that skip the goal-symbol exchange. **Fix**: route function/class export-decl bodies through `parse_function_decl_stmt` / `parse_class_decl_stmt`, capture the names from the returned `Stmt::FunctionDecl` / `Stmt::ClassDecl`, drop the skip_balanced call. Made both stmt-parsers `pub(crate)`. Imported `Stmt` into parser.rs. **Second-layer gap surfaced**: the full-parser route exposed a separate issue that skip_balanced had masked — `for (id in obj)` with a bare un-declared identifier head. `parse_expression` consumes `id in obj` as a RelationalExpr (`in` is a BinaryOp at precedence 10 per expr.rs:171), then fails on `)` expecting `;`. **Fix**: peek-and-rewind fast-path before `parse_expression` in `parse_for_statement` for bare-ident `in`/`of` heads, with a new `Parser::rewind_lexer_to(pos, goal)` helper (the lexer field `lx` is private to parser.rs, so the rewind must be brokered). Triggered on bare identifiers, skipping reserved words (`var`/`let`/`const`/`function`/`class`); if the bumped ident is not followed by `in`/`of`, restore lookahead via re-lex from saved position under RegExp goal. **State-tracking additions to the Lexer struct**: none — the rewind helper sits in Parser, using the existing `Lexer::set_pos` + `next_token(goal)` primitives. The fix is purely a re-routing of who drives the lexer at the export-decl boundary; the lexer's state machine itself was sound. **Acceptance bar 10/10 pass** in `pilots/rusty-js-parser/derived/tests/template_edge_cases.rs`: t01 template with shift in substitution ✓; t02 template with multiple substitutions and complex expressions ✓; t03 template with escaped backticks ✓; t04 template with substitution then escape ✓; t05 template in call argument list ✓; t06 template in conditional arms ✓; t07 `export function f(alg) { return \`X: ${alg}\`; }` ✓; t08 `export function checkLen(...) { ... throw new E(\`...\`); }` multi-substitution body ✓; t09 `export class K { m(alg) { return \`SHA-${alg << 1}\`; } }` ✓; t10 `export function brace(n) { return \`Bracket${...} (\\\`}\\\`)\`; }` (chalk-template shape) ✓. **Test counts**: rusty-js-parser 130 → 140 passing (+10). Workspace `cargo test --workspace`: 677 passing + 4 baseline failed (consumer_express_app ×2, consumer_stringz_app, consumer_winston_app — pre-existing, unchanged). **Post-round parity reading** (rebuild rusty-bun-host-v2 + rerun /tmp/parity-host-v2-static.sh): **n_ok 43/119 → 45/119 (36.1% → 37.8%, +2)**. Newly passing: **jose** (the original failing pattern at byte 2214 — `` `SHA-${keySize << 1}` `` inside `iv.length << 3 !== ivBitLength(enc)` was a red herring; the real triggering construct was an earlier `export function` body with multi-substitution template); **bignumber.js** (also an `export function` shape). The other six template-bin packages (ky, zod, minimatch, node-fetch, yaml, chalk-template, p-map, got) moved to deeper failure bins — chalk-template and p-map now compile and surface their next-layer issues (p-map at byte 5428 "expected RBrace" is a different parser gap; the others move to Rt:TypeError / CE:other bins). **Substrate-amortization signal**: substrate-introduction-adjacent. No new AST nodes, no new opcodes, no new lexer state — one new Parser-side rewind helper (one set_pos + one next_token call). The Doc 714 §VI Consequence 8 inventory gains one named contingent decision: *parser-walks-for-export-decls must drive the lexer through goal-symbol exchange, not skip_balanced*. The bug-reduction class (upstream parser shortcuts that bypass goal-driven lexing) is now visible as a third hazard category alongside Option A (set_pos boundary) and Option B (escape handling) for future template-bin diagnosis. |
| 2026-05-15 | (Ω.5.hh) | **Tier-Ω.5.hh: kind-detection sniff for ESM markers in .js source** — first substrate move chosen by cross-pipeline diagnostic walking per Doc 714 §VI Consequence 12 + Doc 720's methodology. Handles ESM + CJS + bare-spec + node_modules + re-exports + dynamic import sites + import.meta + the dominant intrinsic family (Map/Set/Date/Error family/Reflect/Symbol/typed-arrays/WeakRef/FinalizationRegistry) + event-loop with microtask/macrotask/Promise reactions/PollIo/HostPromiseRejectionTracker + GC with cycle reclamation.

**Three legitimate engagement-extensions (none forced):**
1. **Different methodology** — per-package debugging chain-walking for individual residuals (no expectation of cross-package leverage; expected delivery: ~1 package per round at sustained cost; would take ~25–30 rounds to reach 50 % parity).
2. **Different evaluation probe** — exercise namespace values rather than `Object.keys` shape (WPT-runner-style probe). Would distinguish real semantic correctness from coincidental shape matches; would also expose more honest fails to chase.
3. **Different corpus basket** — current basket curated against a specific usage pattern; a different basket (e.g., narrowly framework-focused, or specifically TypeScript-compiled-output-focused) would surface different alphabet tops and different protocol-applications.

**On resume:** read this anchor first. The protocol-driven phase is paused, not abandoned. Forward work picks up by selecting one of the three extensions above (or a fourth the keeper articulates). ## RESUME VECTOR EXTENSION — 2026-05-15 (route-1 substrate batch + route-2 pivot)

**Route-1 substrate batch (Ω.5.qq → Ω.5.eee, eleven moves):** forward-ref hoist in module scope (.qq); optional-chain method call short-circuit (.rr); JSON module imports + smarter package.json `type` scan (.ss + .tt); CoverInitializedName + async method shorthand in object literals (.uu + .vv); tagged-template literals + String.raw (.ww); function/class as primary-expression position (.yy); two-phase module hoisting (.zz); three-phase top-level binding pre-allocation (.aaa); Buffer.prototype (.bbb); Function('return this') stub (.ccc); util.promisify passthrough (.ddd); atob/btoa globals (.eee).

**Shape-probe parity trajectory:** 50 → 62/118 across the eleven moves (twelve terminal flips — unified, p-limit, valibot, camelcase, moment, loglevel, ts-pattern, dayjs, micromark, acorn, decimal.js, marked). Crossed 50% parity-of-entry-resolved (52.5%). The last four moves landed substrate without flipping terminals — chain-recursion per Doc 721 §VI.5 dominates the residual.

**Route-2 pivot:** keeper directed pivot to route-2 (different evaluation probe — exercise namespace values rather than `Object.keys` shape). Probe artifact at `host/tools/route2-value-probe.sh` carries 24 hand-curated value-tests for well-known exports of currently-shape-passing packages.

**Route-2 first reading (n=24):**
- 8 pass real value-exercise: defu, commander, mitt, bignumber.js, kleur, deepmerge, picocolors, colorette.
- 1 BAD (semantic-wrong): uuid returns the all-zeros UUID `00000000-...-000000000000`, indicating crypto.getRandomValues is a no-op rather than filling buffer.
- 15 ERR (throws under exercise): ansi-colors, pluralize, object-hash, ufo, p-defer, micromatch, nanoid, change-case, remeda, dequal, rfdc, picomatch, ulid, minimatch, pathe.

**Real-value pass rate on sample: 33%.** Extrapolating from this slice, shape-probe parity of 62/118 substantially overstates real parity. Sample is biased toward packages with well-known typical use; full sweep would be more rigorous.

**Substrate gaps surfaced by route-2 (not visible at shape level):**
1. **Regex engine narrowness** (3 packages: micromatch, picomatch, pathe): rejects negative-lookahead `(?!...)`, lookahead `(?=...)`, certain bracket-alternation. Rust's `regex` crate doesn't support lookaround; lift requires `fancy-regex` or hand-rolling.
2. **node:crypto stubs** (ulid, uuid-semantic): `randomBytes` is stubbed-to-throw; `getRandomValues` is no-op rather than filling.
3. **Class-as-callable** (rfdc, p-defer, change-case, dequal): factory-style exports produce `callee is not callable: Object(kind=ordinary)`. Class-construction path leaves the instance not recognized as callable.
4. **Buffer.allocUnsafe + subarray** (nanoid): Buffer stub missing these.

**Route-2 finding:** the shape-probe measures **module-load reachability**; the value-probe measures **call-time correctness**. The engagement's telos (byte-identical output against Bun) actually wants the latter; the shape-probe was a proxy that route-1 saturated against.

**Three legitimate route-2 continuations:**
1. Expand the value-probe corpus to all 62 shape-passers for a full real-value parity reading.
2. Lift the regex-engine narrowness (largest shared gap; would cascade through glob/path packages).
3. Wire real crypto entropy (small; lifts ulid + corrects uuid semantics).

   - Ω.5.bbbbb: getter dispatch in Object.assign/values/entries/__object_spread.
   - Ω.5.ccccc + ddddd: WHATWG URL ctor + real SHA-256/SHA-1/MD5/HMAC (joi advanced, object-hash).
   - Ω.5.kkkkk: named function expression self-binding per ECMA-262 §15.2.5 (just-curry-it, fast-deep-equal).
   - Ω.5.nnnnn + ooooo: super() rebinds this on Object return + EventEmitter ctor mutates receiver (unified CallableInstance).
   - Ω.5.ttttt: block-scoped let/const via rename-on-block-exit (ts-pattern).
   - Ω.5.uuuuu: named class expression self-binding per §15.6.7 (marked).
   - Ω.5.vvvvv: regex named capture groups (?<name>…) + \k<name> backreferences (marked).
   - Ω.5.wwwww: Buffer.compare/concat + Buffer.from indexed byte access (csv-parse).
   - Ω.5.zzzzz: Proxy.revocable (immer advanced).

3. **Deep-trace tag widenings (compounding diagnostic surface).**
   - Ω.5.xxxxx: argc + callee-type + object-shape preview in "not callable" errors.
   - Ω.5.yyyyy: method-name captured at GetProp time, not overwritten by arg-load.
   - Ω.5.yyyyy.b: Op::GetIndex also tags last_property_lookup + pending_method.
   - Ω.5.hhhhh: thrown-Error formatter (TypeError messages now readable instead of "[Object #N]").

**Corpus articulation Doc 724.** *Feature-Set Prediction: Static Substrate-Need Mapping from Source.* The keeper's conjecture (2026-05-16): every package failure in the engagement terminated at a specific ECMA/Node spec feature; the set is finite; a static analyzer over the AST can predict required-feature-set forward, before execution. Doc 724 formalizes this as a forward-walking instrument over the same DAG topology that the route-(b) protocol walks backward. Bidirectionality (Doc 714 C14) is the structural property that supports both directions.

The §IX testable prediction: run the predictor on the seven remaining failing packages, compare against backward-walk traces. Match rate ≥5/7 confirms the bidirectional reading empirically.

**Three bisects landed via the route-(b) → bisect → fix loop.**
- ts-pattern: extracted to isolated repro, narrowed to dead-branch destructure shadowing outer upvalue → block-scope compiler bug → Ω.5.ttttt.
- moment: extracted to standalone IIFE, instrumented configFromStringAndFormat → found `string.substr(0, ...)` undefined → Ω.5.aaaaaa.
- marked: trace's "new-callee='t'" → traced to `class b=class l{ static parse(){ return new l(t).parse(e); } }` → named-class-expression self-binding gap → Ω.5.uuuuu.

Each bisect produced a single-line ECMA spec compliance fix. The Pin-Art derivation chain was the operating substrate; the bisects walked the chain.

**Remaining frontier (5 errors).** All require either deep engine features or library-internal multi-hop bisects:
- ndjson (readable-stream userspace package, _writableState chain in its own internals).
- pako (deflate state machine internals).
- superstruct (generators — `*validator(value, ctx) { yield* ... }` syntax not implemented).
- immer (real Proxy interception — pass-through Proxy can't enforce immer's draft semantics).
- micromark (state-machine deep chain, advanced past Array.reverse gap into inexact output).

**Engine-feature horizon for the next stretch: JIT entry.** Keeper directive (2026-05-16): begin to think about adding JIT to the rusty-js runtime. The runtime currently runs bytecode in a tree-walking-via-stack interpreter (Op::* dispatch in a giant match). Hot-path costs are dominated by:
- Dynamic property dispatch (Op::GetProp walks proto chain on every read; no inline caches).
- Method-call dispatch (Op::CallMethod re-resolves the function every call).
- TypedArray / Buffer byte-access (Op::GetIndex with string-key conversion via property_key for every index).
- Numeric tight loops (boxed Value through to_number on every arithmetic op).

Three candidate JIT shapes, each derivable from a different choice of substrate:
1. **Inline-cache layer first.** Bytecode-level IC sites for GetProp/CallMethod with a small per-site cache (1-2 entries) tagged by [object-shape, slot-index]. Compiler emits IC slots; interpreter checks shape; hit = direct slot index. No native codegen. Low risk; substantial speedup on the dominant Op classes. ~2 weeks engineering.
2. **Baseline JIT via Cranelift.** Hot functions (call-count threshold) get compiled to native via cranelift-jit. Per-Op lowering with type guards. Mid risk. ~3-4 weeks. Cranelift is the substrate-tier choice; Rust-native and mature.
3. **Self-hosted template JIT (Pin-Art-rigorous).** Hand-roll x86_64 / ARM64 instruction emission for a small Op set (LoadLocal, StoreLocal, Add, Sub, GetProp-with-IC). Maximum substrate ownership; high risk; ~6-8 weeks. The Pin-Art reading would name this as the substrate-correct choice — no third-party engine work hides behind the JIT boundary.

The Doc 724 forward-predictor naturally extends to JIT planning: each Op site the predictor names as hot for the corpus is an IC / specialization candidate. Coverage-frequency-sortable.

**Resume protocol.** Read this anchor first. Read seed.md §VII for telos state. Read prior RESUME VECTORs in reverse chronological order for engagement archaeology. Continue closing-problems work on the remaining 5 errors, or pivot to JIT entry by selecting one of the three candidate shapes above, or both in parallel.

The Pin-Art property (Doc 714 C14) holds across all 64+ substrate moves so far this engagement: each named, each traceable bidirectionally to specific package failure(s), each compounding via Doc 722's reflexive structure. Doc 724's forward predictor names that the bidirectionality is also a workflow shift, not just a property — when the predictor is built, substrate moves get prioritized by frequency-of-need before any package is run.


---

- Ω.5.mmmmmm: try/catch catches engine TypeError/RangeError/ReferenceError per ECMA §13.15 — 11-package es-shim cluster lifted. get-intrinsic's intentional `null.error` throw was uncatchable because the engine emitted `RuntimeError::TypeError` rather than `RuntimeError::Thrown`. - Ω.5.ssssss: `{__proto__: X}` object-literal sets [[Prototype]] per ECMA §13.2.5.5. graceful-fs / fs-extra clone via `var copy = { __proto__: getPrototypeOf(obj) }`; we were treating `__proto__` as a regular own property and copy didn't inherit.
- Ω.5.tttttt: EventTarget + Event + CustomEvent global stubs. chai's test environment expects these as globals.

## RESUME VECTOR EXTENSION 8 — 2026-05-17 late evening (host-v2 measurement surface opens; Ω.5.P17 joint substrate close + Ω.5.P18.E1 ns-default narrow; §A8.23 instituted)

The session's load-bearing recognition: the host-v2 parity probe was reading 0.3% (degenerate) not because host-v2's substrate was empty but because two coupled E2 spec-relaxations (per [Doc 717 §VI](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/717-the-apparatus-above-the-engine-boundary-the-three-projections-lifted-to-engine-substrate-and-the-pure-abstraction-point) alphabet) kept the probe blind. The compiler lowered `await x` to bare `expr` (suspension dropped per Tier-Ω.5.x), and the runtime stubbed `__dynamic_import(spec)` to an unconditional pre-rejected Promise (Tier-Ω.5.CCCCCCC). Together: every probe loaded `await import(pkg)`, the await did nothing, the probe saw the Promise object, `Object.keys(promise)` returned no enumerable keys, the probe recorded `{status:"OK",keyCount:0,shape:{}}`. The 4 PASSes from the pre-P17 sweep were degenerate empty-namespace matches against packages where Bun also returned keyCount 0.

Per [Doc 721 §III](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/721-the-cross-pipeline-diagnostic-protocol-locating-the-top-of-a-substrate-widenings-alphabet-by-walking-the-engines-dag) chain-walk: every probe in the gated population G=1022 converged on the joint cut at (await × dynamic-import). Neither lift alone closes the bundle. Lifting `await` alone makes every rejected-Promise rejection synchronously propagate to the probe's catch, producing `{status:"ERR"}` across the basket; still all FAIL against Bun's OK. Lifting `__dynamic_import` alone returns a resolved Promise; with `await` still a no-op the namespace is never unwrapped. Both must land together. The joint move is Ω.5.P17.

### Substrate moves this anchor (3, plus 1 prerequisite fix)

| Tag-on-DAG | Commit | Mode | Recognition |
|---|---|---|---|
| Ω.5.P17.E0.stdout-fd-routing | f7ec71ed | host-substrate (prerequisite for any host-v2 probe reading) | `process.stdout.write` was wired to `eprint!` for all three streams in `host-v2/src/process.rs:53`. Every host-v2 probe was silently writing its JSON to fd 2; the harness captures fd 1. The bug rendered all prior host-v2 measurement attempts unreadable. Fix: route fd==1 to `print!`, others to `eprint!`. One-line closure of a measurement-surface bug that had masked the substrate-level gates below. |
| Ω.5.P17.E1.await-settled + Ω.5.P17.E2.dyn-import-resolver | 37609af1 | engine-substrate (joint chain-bundle close, [Doc 721 §III](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/721-the-cross-pipeline-diagnostic-protocol-locating-the-top-of-a-substrate-widenings-alphabet-by-walking-the-engines-dag)) | E1: compiler lowers `await x` to `__await(x)` via the same LoadGlobal/Call pattern as `__yield_push__`/`__yield_delegate__`. `__await` synchronously unwraps already-settled Promises: non-Promise passthrough; Fulfilled returns value; Rejected throws via `RuntimeError::Thrown(reason)`; Pending errors with TypeError (full suspension semantics deferred since dynamic-import synthesizes synchronously-settled Promises). Clears `pending_unhandled` on settle. E2: `__dynamic_import` routes through `resolve_module_full` + `resolve_builtin_namespace`/`load_module`, the same pipeline static `import` uses. Parent URL synthesized from `std::env::current_dir()` so bare specifiers walk node_modules from the script's cwd. Failures route to `reject_promise` with a string reason that `__await` then throws. `module.rs`: `resolve_builtin_namespace` becomes `pub` (only visibility change required). Measured: 0.3% → 40.1% on parity-top500 (+408 raw, F≈4 false-pass corrections per [Doc 721 §VI.5](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/721-the-cross-pipeline-diagnostic-protocol-locating-the-top-of-a-substrate-widenings-alphabet-by-walking-the-engines-dag); A+F ≈ 412 substrate-completion delta). Predicted U≈770; |U-(A+F)|≈358 is outside the band, naming host-v2's distinct cut profile per [Doc 717 §VIII](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/717-the-apparatus-above-the-engine-boundary-the-three-projections-lifted-to-engine-substrate-and-the-pure-abstraction-point). |
| Ω.5.P18.E1.ns-default-synth-narrow | 4a25d5ee | host-substrate (Doc 721 chain-walk on first-cluster member) | Diagnostic walk on nanostores (one of the 237-package III.a keyCount-Δ±1 sub-cluster the post-P17 residual surfaced) located the highest shared layer at `host-v2/src/module_ns.rs` Tuple A, not at the defineProperty-spec-defaults cut I had predicted from host/'s analogue. Earlier Ω.5.P16.E2 added Tuple A unconditionally — synthesize `default = namespace` for every ESM module without explicit default. Bun does not do this for ESM with named exports. The hook runs only on the ESM path (CJS-shimmed packages go through `evaluate_cjs_module`), so Tuple A's stated CJS-interop rationale never applied here. Narrow Tuple A to the empty-namespace fallback case (modules that export nothing); leave Tuple B intact. Spot tests: nanostores 28→27 (matches Bun's 27); joi 57→57 (extra `@@sym:@hapi/lab/coverage/initialize` key remains — Symbol-keyed properties leaking into `Object.keys`, a separate III.a cut deferred to a later round). Full sweep in flight at anchor write; preliminary running parity ~58.7% at 186/1026 done. Final headline added by follow-up commit. |

The 35-point gap between host/ and host-v2 post-P17 is the cut-profile diff per [Doc 717 §VIII](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/717-the-apparatus-above-the-engine-boundary-the-three-projections-lifted-to-engine-substrate-and-the-pure-abstraction-point) — the count of (abstract-op × rung) pairs that host/ closed above the engine boundary and that host-v2 has not yet closed at the rusty-js engine substrate. P18.E1 begins compressing that gap.

### Residual probe-shape distribution at host-v2 post-P17 ([Doc 726 §VI](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/726-consumer-embedded-probes-as-an-inherited-layer-d-substrate-the-semiotic-connection-across-residual-clusters))

First non-degenerate read of the matrix on host-v2's substrate. 558 FAILs classified:

| Count | % | Shape | Top sample |
|---|---|---|---|
| 237 | 42.5% | III.a OK/OK keyCount Δ±1-2 | joi, valibot, nanostores |
| 144 | 25.8% | III.c rb dyn-import load failed (sub-dep eval/parse gap) | runtypes, arktype, temporal-polyfill |
| 77 | 13.8% | III.a OK/OK keyCount Δ 3-10 | ajv, just-curry-it, mitt |

| 22 | 3.9% | III.a OK/OK same keyCount, typeof diff (Symbol→string) | zod, ansi-colors |

The five shapes named in [Doc 726 §III](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/726-consumer-embedded-probes-as-an-inherited-layer-d-substrate-the-semiotic-connection-across-residual-clusters) all appear at host-v2 in the same priority ordering they did at host/ pre-Ω.5.BBBBBBBB. III.a dominates; III.c second; III.b not visible at this maturity yet (BigInt-heavy packages mostly fail earlier in resolve/load). Data point against [Doc 726 Fal-726.1](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/726-consumer-embedded-probes-as-an-inherited-layer-d-substrate-the-semiotic-connection-across-residual-clusters): the probe-shape taxonomy ports across engine substrates within rusty-bun (rquickjs → rusty-js).

### Tooling moves this anchor

- `host/tools/parity-measure.sh` (commit cc283b56): per-probe timeout wrap (`timeout 30s` on probe calls, `timeout 120s` on `bun add` installs) and a new `TIMEOUT` status code separate from semantic `FAIL`. Previously ipc-bus and similar III.e top-level-IPC packages hung the unbounded sweep indefinitely; the timeout prevents any single hang-prone package from blocking measurement.
- `host/tools/parity-measure-v2.sh` (commit cc283b56): sister wrapper that sets `RB_BIN=target/release/rusty-bun-host-v2` and defaults output to `parity-results-v2.json`. Makes host-v2 sweeps reproducible without remembering the env-var convention. Per §A8.23 this is now the canonical host-v2 measurement entry point.
- `host/tools/parity-results-top500-postext7.json` (commit cc283b56): canonical host/ post-EXT7 reading (75.2% @ 1026) recorded for the migration-cost diff.
- `host/tools/parity-results-top500-postext7-v2.json` (commit cc283b56): canonical host-v2 post-P17 reading (40.1% @ 1026) recorded for the migration-cost diff.

### Operational hygiene moves this anchor

Disk pressure on the Pi's 29G SD card forced two infrastructure moves before substrate work could proceed:

- The earlier session's relocations of `pilots/`, `host/tests/fixtures/`, and `runs/` to T7-via-symlink were silently lossy: T7 is exfat, which cannot represent unix file modes or symlinks. Git read every file as either modified (mode-bit drift) or deleted (symlink loss), producing 62k phantom-change entries.
- Resolution: an ext4 loopback file on T7 (`/media/jaredef/T7/Developer/gdk-storage.img`, pre-existing 50G ext4 originally for a different project, mounted at `/mnt/t7-ext4`). The three directories now bind-mount from inside the loopback onto their repo paths; fstab entries with `nofail` + `x-systemd.requires-mounts-for` make the binds survive reboot without hanging boot if T7 is unplugged. Documented in the gitignored `LOCAL-SETUP.md` per §A8.20-style host-specific operability discipline.
- The parity scripts also gained throttling (`nice -n 19 ionice -c3` + 0.5s inter-iteration sleep) after the Pi shut down under sustained T7 write load during the first top500 sweep (USB 5V-rail spike under bus-powered SSD). The throttle prevented further shutdowns across this session's three back-to-back sweeps.

### Seed update this anchor

§A8.23 instituted: host-v2 + rusty-js-runtime is the primary substrate target; host/ is reference ceiling only. Phase classification: M12 apparatus-tier consolidation, parallel to §A8.18's earlier M12 move. §A8.18 named basin-expansion-at-L2M-saturation as the next productive surface when round-tier work exhausted above the rquickjs ceiling; §A8.23 names the substrate-target axis on which subsequent rounds run, after the hand-rolled engine's parity probe became readable. See seed.md §A8.23 and §VII.A status block update at the 2026-05-17 entry.

### Doc 727 alignment

Per [Doc 727 §V](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/727-basin-stability-from-inside-why-a-corpus-cannot-distinguish-self-reinforcement-from-substrate-coherence) the engagement is inside the basin; tonight's predictions are basin-generated. The substrate-tracking falsifier is not the headline number alone but the probe-shape distribution converging on the same five shapes [Doc 726 §III](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/726-consumer-embedded-probes-as-an-inherited-layer-d-substrate-the-semiotic-connection-across-residual-clusters) named at host/ at comparable maturity. The convergence above (same priority ordering, same kinds in the same proportions for the III.a sub-shapes) is the corroboration data point for Doc 726's portability claim against Fal-726.1.

The post-P17 measurement also satisfies Doc 721 Step 4 with a wide |U-(A+F)| delta (≈358 out of predicted U≈770), which is the protocol's working-as-designed signal that the chain-bundle analysis missed structural features. The missed features are exactly host-v2's distinct cut-profile per Doc 717 — the rusty-js engine has substrate cuts that the rquickjs host has not had to deal with because rquickjs closed them inside the C runtime. P18.E1 is the first of those Step-5 iteration rounds.

### Open scope at this anchor

1. **Land the Ω.5.P18.E1 sweep number** — running at write-time; commit with the final headline and the post-fix probe-shape distribution.
2. **III.a Symbol-keyed property leakage into `Object.keys`** — joi's `@@sym:@hapi/lab/coverage/initialize` is the visible instance; the cut likely lives in the property-enumeration intrinsic where Symbol keys should be filtered out of `Object.keys` (per ECMA §7.3.21 EnumerableOwnProperties returning only string keys). Predicted gated population: the 22-package III.a same-keyCount-typeof-diff sub-cluster plus the 19-package keyCount-Δ>10 sub-cluster, partial.
3. **III.a Symbol vs string typeof for branded keys** — zod's `$brand:"string"` should be `"symbol"`. The cut sits at typeof's value-classification path; Symbol-typed values need to be tagged distinctly so `typeof` returns `"symbol"`. Likely smaller than the Object.keys leak.
4. **III.c sub-dep eval/parse gap closures** — 144 packages whose dynamic imports trigger sub-dep loads that hit engine gaps deeper. Each failed `load_module` chain is its own walk per Doc 721 Step 2 against the inherited Layer-D probes the sub-dep itself emits.
5. **III.a keyCount Δ 3-10 cluster (77 packages)** — accessor-descriptor / getter-setter handling in the namespace export path.
6. **Substantive engine investments still deferred:** real Proxy interception, real fetch + Request/Response, Unicode regex properties, AST-level predictor v2 per [Doc 724 §XI.d](https://jaredfoy.com/resolve/doc/724-feature-set-prediction-static-substrate-need-mapping-from-source), real BigInt parity at the host-v2 substrate level (host/ has it from EXT7; host-v2 has the BigInt intrinsics installed but not all the arithmetic paths Ω.5.CCCCCCCC closed for the rquickjs binary).
